  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>When reading in seq2sparse output from HDFS in the spark-shell of form &lt;Text,VectorWriteable&gt; SparkEngine's drmFromHDFS method is creating rdds with the same Key for all Pairs: </p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">mahout&gt; val drmTFIDF= drmFromHDFS( path = <span class="code-quote">"/tmp/mahout-work-andy/20news-test-vectors/part-r-00000"</span>)
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>Has keys:</p> {...} 
                  <br> key: /talk.religion.misc/84570
                  <br> key: /talk.religion.misc/84570
                  <br> key: /talk.religion.misc/84570
                  <br> {...} 
                  <p>for the entire set. This is the last Key in the set.</p> 
                  <p>The problem can be traced to the first line of drmFromHDFS(...) in SparkEngine.scala: </p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java"> val rdd = sc.sequenceFile(path, classOf[Writable], classOf[VectorWritable], minPartitions = parMin)
        <span class="code-comment">// Get rid of VectorWritable
</span>        .map(t =&gt; (t._1, t._2.get()))
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>which gives the same key for all t._1.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>
              <div id="dnd-metadata" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="dnd-metadata_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>

              <div id="activitymodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="activitymodule_heading" class="mod-header">

So what Matei is saying there, should not already be applicable.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    More likely, i was thinking, spark is creating a strict collection when it fuses two maps, so more likely fix would be simply removing extra map, something along the lines \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e         val rdd = sc.sequenceFile(path, classOf\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;Writable&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e, classOf\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;VectorWritable&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e, minPartitions = parMin)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e        ... \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e          val drmRdd = rdd.map \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n{ t =&gt; key2valFunc(t._1) -&gt; t._2.get}\\n\u003cp\u003e        ...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    (so there\'s no forced map fusion). But it doesn\'t seem to work in my tests either.  Weird.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    Ok i think i want to stop spending my neurons on this for now and  to have a look at it tomorrow again. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    But i don\'t think we should clone anything. we just need to transform away from writable before attempting any caches.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"githubbot\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14133581_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=githubbot\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"githubbot\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e ASF GitHub Bot\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14133581_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'15\\/Sep\\/14 04:52\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2014-09-15T04:52:39+0000\'\u003e15\\/Sep\\/14 04:52\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Github user dlyubimov commented on the pull request: \\n\\n      https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/52#issuecomment-55552838  \\n\\n     yeah i dont think cloning is needed, since we unwrapping the actual object (string, int etc). class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2014-09-15T17:39:42+0000\'\u003e15\\/Sep\\/14 17:39\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eGithub user dlyubimov commented on the pull request:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/52#issuecomment-55627685\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttps:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/52#issuecomment-55627685\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    Well, there are three solutions to the problem I see. One is easy, another is pretty easy but perhaps more expensive operationally.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    First, let\'s clarify what is going on there. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    (1) since the key type is having a ContextTag as context bound: DrmLike type is defined as DrmLike\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;K:ClassTag&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e, it means that returning CheckpointedDrm\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;_&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e (which is subtype) from drmFromHDFS in fact implicitly means returning two things: CheckpointedDrm and evidence:ContextTag\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;K&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e. The evidence is essentially a run time class information (including all generics hierarchies possibly attached to it).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    Thinking is, since key class name is stored in the sequence file headers, it makes sense to expect for this routine to read out the header and infer ContextTag\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;K&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e on its own. As comment indicates there, it actually expected Spark to do that. But simple examination of sequenceFile() reveals that Spark actually does not do that. Instead, it is just propagates the evidence it already got when this method is called, and doesn\'t read any headers (or anything for that matter) until actual execution action occurs. As a result, intended conversion from writable to its wrapped type (String, Int or Long) does not really happen as it stands; instead, Writable is just propagated up the food chain, and we of course already know that writable instances are reused and would not make it thru strict Scala collections. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    So, based on that, there are two ways to address that. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    (1) One, simple way, is to escape this problem the same way Spark has escaped it: namely, require actual key type evidence from the user. That would require changing method signature to \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e       def drmFromHDFS\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;K:ClassTag&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e (path: String, parMin:Int = 0)(implicit sc: DistributedContext): CheckpointedDrm\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;K&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    Then you\'d have to implicitly supply evidence by doing something like this:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e        val drmA:DrmLike\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;String&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e = drmFromHdfs(...)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    I don\'t like this too much. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    First, you have to remember to explicitly give it a type like above instead of implicit type inference which is expected in Scala \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e         val drmA=...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    Another reason i don\'t like it is that you potentially are supplying a redundant information (since this information is already available form sequence file headers). Not only that, you \u003cem\u003ehave\u003c\\/em\u003e to be right, or your delayed execution will fail in the tasks (so it is late error catching, which is fairly hairy for most users, so i\'d expect a wall of questions of the type \\\"why my tasks fail\\\" for this very basic operation. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    So, not so user-friendly (although those who know will cope). \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    (2) Another way to fix it is to keep current method contract, and fill in this functionality that I believe is missing in Spark, namely, examine input headers and load in key class type and thus infer proper ClassTag\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;_&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    There practically no downsides to this, except for one. Up until now we pretty much avoided direct dependencies on any Hadoop libraries. Spark goes to great length (mostly, reflection and pluggable Strategies based on Hadoop version) in order to retain compatibility with various HDFS flavors and versions. I just don\'t want to join this game. Very much so.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    (3) Another way is similar to (2) in the sense that we keep the signature and idea of filling the gap of inferring ClassTag\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;_&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e ourselves, but we do it by examining first Writeable key instance in the dataset. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    This is even better than (2) since it keeps us from dealing with HDFS apis directly. But obvious downside is that we probably now will have to load the entire partition in spark instead of just reading sequence file header. So much for delayed action and memory allocation. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003chr \\/\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003e    my personal preference is probably going with (2) while exploring (3) in terms of how bad this practice actually may get. Of course (1) is also an option since it is the easiest to implement.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"githubbot\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14134174_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=githubbot\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"githubbot\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e ASF GitHub Bot\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14134174_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'15\\/Sep\\/14 17:39\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2014-09-15T17:39:42+0000\'\u003e15\\/Sep\\/14 17:39\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Github user dlyubimov commented on the pull request: \\n\\n      https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/52#issuecomment-55627685  \\n\\n     Well, there are three solutions to the problem I see. One is easy, another is pretty easy but perhaps more expensive operationally. \\n\\n     First, let\'s clarify what is going on there.  \\n\\n     (1) since the key type is having a ContextTag as context bound: DrmLike type is defined as DrmLike &#91;K:ClassTag&#93; , it means that returning CheckpointedDrm &#91;_&#93;  (which is subtype) from drmFromHDFS in fact implicitly means returning two things: CheckpointedDrm and evidence:ContextTag &#91;K&#93; . The evidence is essentially a run time class information (including all generics hierarchies possibly attached to it). \\n\\n     Thinking is, since key class name is stored in the sequence file headers, it makes sense to expect for this routine to read out the header and infer ContextTag &#91;K&#93;  on its own. As comment indicates there, it actually expected Spark to do that. But simple examination of sequenceFile() reveals that Spark actually does not do that. Instead, it is just propagates the evidence it already got when this method is called, and doesn\'t read any headers (or anything for that matter) until actual execution action occurs. As a result, intended conversion from writable to its wrapped type (String, Int or Long) does not really happen as it stands; instead, Writable is just propagated up the food chain, and we of course already know that writable instances are reused and would not make it thru strict Scala collections.  \\n\\n     So, based on that, there are two ways to address that.  \\n\\n     (1) One, simple way, is to escape this problem the same way Spark has escaped it: namely, require actual key type evidence from the user. That would require changing method signature to  \\n\\n        def drmFromHDFS &#91;K:ClassTag&#93;  (path: String, parMin:Int = 0)(implicit sc: DistributedContext): CheckpointedDrm &#91;K&#93;   \\n\\n\\n     Then you\'d have to implicitly supply evidence by doing something like this: \\n\\n         val drmA:DrmLike &#91;String&#93;  = drmFromHdfs(...) \\n\\n     I don\'t like this too much.  \\n\\n     First, you have to remember to explicitly give it a type like above instead of implicit type inference which is expected in Scala  \\n\\n          val drmA=... \\n\\n     Another reason i don\'t like it is that you potentially are supplying a redundant information (since this information is already available form sequence file headers). Not only that, you  have  to be right, or your delayed execution will fail in the tasks (so it is late error catching, which is fairly hairy for most users, so i\'d expect a wall of questions of the type \\\"why my tasks fail\\\" for this very basic operation.  \\n\\n     So, not so user-friendly (although those who know will cope).  \\n\\n     (2) Another way to fix it is to keep current method contract, and fill in this functionality that I believe is missing in Spark, namely, examine input headers and load in key class type and thus infer proper ClassTag &#91;_&#93; .  \\n\\n     There practically no downsides to this, except for one. Up until now we pretty much avoided direct dependencies on any Hadoop libraries. Spark goes to great length (mostly, reflection and pluggable Strategies based on Hadoop version) in order to retain compatibility with various HDFS flavors and versions. I just don\'t want to join this game. Very much so. \\n\\n     (3) Another way is similar to (2) in the sense that we keep the signature and idea of filling the gap of inferring ClassTag &#91;_&#93;  ourselves, but we do it by examining first Writeable key instance in the dataset.  \\n\\n     This is even better than (2) since it keeps us from dealing with HDFS apis directly. But obvious downside is that we probably now will have to load the entire partition in spark instead of just reading sequence file header. So much for delayed action and memory allocation.  \\n\\n\\n \\n     my personal preference is probably going with (2) while exploring (3) in terms of how bad this practice actually may get. Of course (1) is also an option since it is the easiest to implement.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n Examples of what it means : \\n\\n\\n          def method &#91;K:ContextType&#93; ( ...params) \\n\\n\\n     is equivalent to declaring \\n\\n         def method(...params)(implicit evidence$1:ContextType) \\n\\n\\n     similarly, \\n\\n         class Clazz &#91;K:ContextType&#93;  (...params...) \\n\\n\\n     is equivalent to writing \\n\\n         class Clazz(...params...)(implicit val evidence$1:ContextType)  .... \\n\\n\\n     so when you do what you did it is equivalent to returning implicitly passed \\n    parameter to the mehod, not implicit value extraction from implementation \\n    class you\'ve passed. \\n\\n\\n\\n     On Mon, Sep 22, 2014 at 9:58 AM, Dmitriy Lyubimov &lt;dlieu.7@gmail.com&gt; wrote: \\n\\n     &gt; on (1), it doesn\'t work because it takes classTag from the method bound, \\n    &gt; not from actual evidence in the class. \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; in order for this to work, i suggest to add \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; def keyClassTag:ClassTag &#91;K&#93;  \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; to CheckpointedDrm trait and implement it in concrete checkpoined \\n    &gt; implementations as simply `implicitly[ClassTag &#91;K&#93; ]`. Unfortunately you \\n    &gt; cannot implement it in a trait (like inside DrmLike or CheckpointedDRM) \\n    &gt; because as it stands, traits do not support access to concrete class \\n    &gt; evidence (as our workaround demonstrates, it is theoretically possible to \\n    &gt; support it thru virtual query to implementation, but as it stands, scala is \\n    &gt; not really there). \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; on (2), you need to ask to load not the directory, by any partition file \\n    &gt; inside that directory. This is \\n    &gt; why i am saying implementing it with full cross-version hadoop \\n    &gt; compatibility the way Spark does is extremely hairy. \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; On Mon, Sep 22, 2014 at 9:36 AM, Andrew Palumbo &lt;notifications@github.com&gt; \\n    &gt; wrote: \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt;&gt; Still a work in progress, (and still in need of some cleanup). \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eGithub user dlyubimov commented on the pull request:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/52#issuecomment-56920785\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttps:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/52#issuecomment-56920785\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    I think the more standard types we support the better. Original Mahout DRM concept did not assume any sort of limitations on key type. It could be a tree, for all we know. The limitation stems from trying to build higher-level subroutines like drmFromHDFS for the algebraic optimizer, where user is not assumed to supply writeable to value converter on its own; at least, not by default. Maybe we just need an additional version of drmFromHDFS where such conversion function could be supplied explicitly by the user in order to handle compound annotation key types such as trees or  collections.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    The reason why int, long and String were chosen as necessary minimum conversion set of types  is mostly because there are known algorithms that rely on these types. String is used in seq2sparse output, Int has a special meaning for transposition, and Long... Long happens from time to time in legacy Mahout code too.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e     The idea with implicit converters was to support anything that is already defined in implicit scope, without match. Think about it. Implicit stuff is just a special case of a scope. Like a package. as such, it might be possible to enumerate those conversions at runtime. Unfortunately I haven\'t found a scala construct that would allow to do that and apply found conversion elegantly. so this point is probably just a distraction. Let\'s forget about it and perhaps assume a match for a set of basic types, as defined in Spark. We should require hard stop if we don\'t know the converter (and user hasn\'t supplied one).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"githubbot\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14148797_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=githubbot\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"githubbot\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e ASF GitHub Bot\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14148797_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'26\\/Sep\\/14 05:27\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2014-09-26T05:27:22+0000\'\u003e26\\/Sep\\/14 05:27\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Github user dlyubimov commented on the pull request: \\n\\n      https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/52#issuecomment-56920785  \\n\\n     I think the more standard types we support the better. Original Mahout DRM concept did not assume any sort of limitations on key type. It could be a tree, for all we know. The limitation stems from trying to build higher-level subroutines like drmFromHDFS for the algebraic optimizer, where user is not assumed to supply writeable to value converter on its own; at least, not by default. Maybe we just need an additional version of drmFromHDFS where such conversion function could be supplied explicitly by the user in order to handle compound annotation key types such as trees or  collections. \\n\\n     The reason why int, long and String were chosen as necessary minimum conversion set of types  is mostly because there are known algorithms that rely on these types. String is used in seq2sparse output, Int has a special meaning for transposition, and Long... Long happens from time to time in legacy Mahout code too. \\n\\n      The idea with implicit converters was to support anything that is already defined in implicit scope, without match. Think about it. Implicit stuff is just a special case of a scope. Like a package. as such, it might be possible to enumerate those conversions at runtime. Unfortunately I haven\'t found a scala construct that would allow to do that and apply found conversion elegantly. so this point is probably just a distraction. Let\'s forget about it and perhaps assume a match for a set of basic types, as defined in Spark. We should require hard stop if we don\'t know the converter (and user hasn\'t supplied one). \\n\\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-14149734\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/MAHOUT-1615?focusedCommentId=14149734&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-14149734\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"githubbot\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14149734_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=githubbot\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"githubbot\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e ASF GitHub Bot\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  -
